The GT has these basis functions:
1. `x**3` term
2. `x*exp(-Abs(x))` term
3. `sin(t)` term
4. `sin(v)` term

Key observations:
- The GT contains `sin(t)`, which can be written as `cos(t - π/2)`, so `cos(c + t)` can match this.
- The GT contains `sin(v)`, which is NOT the same as any polynomial in `v`, `v*Abs(v)`, `v**3`, `v**5`, etc.
- The GT contains `x*exp(-Abs(x))`, which is NOT a polynomial, NOT `x*Abs(x)`, and cannot be represented by polynomials or `x*Abs(x)`.

**Critical issue:** The term `-sin(v)` cannot be exactly represented by combinations of `v`, `v**3`, `v**5`, `v*Abs(v)`, or any polynomial/piecewise-polynomial basis in `v`. These are linearly independent functions.

Similarly, `x*exp(-Abs(x))` cannot be exactly represented by `x*Abs(x)`, polynomials in `x`, or any combination thereof. The function `exp(-Abs(x))` is fundamentally different from polynomial or piecewise-polynomial functions.

Let me check all candidates systematically:

**Every single candidate** uses some combination of:
- `cos(c + t)` for the time dependence ✓ (can match `sin(t)`)
- Polynomial terms in `v`: `v`, `v**3`, `v**5`, `v*Abs(v)`, or `v**c` — these **cannot** exactly equal `sin(v)` ✗
- For the `x` terms: `x*Abs(x)`, `x**3`, `x**5`, `x**7`, `x**c`, `x*Abs(x)` — these **cannot** exactly equal `x*exp(-Abs(x))` ✗

For candidates with `v**c4` (like Candidate 14, 36): `v**c4` is a power function, not `sin(v)`. No single power can equal `sin(v)`.

For Candidate 33 with `x/(c1 + x**2)`: This is a rational function, not `x*exp(-Abs(x))`.

**None of the candidates** contain `sin(v)` or `exp(-Abs(x))` or any functions that could be equivalent to these. Since `sin(v)` is linearly independent from all polynomials and piecewise polynomials in `v`, and `x*exp(-Abs(x))` is linearly independent from all polynomials and `x*Abs(x)`, no candidate can match the GT.
